from resetting the\n    40→  // pointer: If we just set latest to current, then the first onData filter iteration would\n    41→  // correctly iterate over the filters and set latest, but on We first see\n  // if the stream needs to be reset. If it needs to be, this will end up invoking reset callbacks\n  // and then moving the stream to the deferred destruction list. If the stream has not been reset,\n  // we move it to the deferred deletion list here. Then, we potentially close the connection. This\n  // must be done after deleting the stream since the stream refers to the connection and must be\n  // deleted first.\n  bool reset_stream = false;\n  // If the response encoder is still associated with the stream, reset the stream. !stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_)) {\n    // Indicate local is complete at this point so that if we reset during a continuation, we don't\n    // raise further data or trailers.\n    ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(debug, \"doEndStream() resetting stream\", stream);\n    // TODO(snowp): This call might not be necessary, try to clean up + remove setter function.\n    stream.filter_manager_.setLocalComplete();\n    stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_ = true;\n\n    // Per https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7540#section-8.3 if there was an error\n    // with the TCP     StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamConnectionTermination))) {\n      stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ConnectError);\n    } else {\n      const bool reset_with_error =\n          Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\"envoy.reloadable_features.reset_with_error\");\n      if (stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\n              StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::UpstreamProtocolError) &&\n          !Runtime::runtimeFeatureEnabled(\n              \"envoy.reloadable_features.reset_ignore_upstream_reason\")) {\n        stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ProtocolError);\n      } else if (reset_with_error && stream.filter_manager_.streamInfo().hasResponseFlag(\n                                         StreamInfo::CoreResponseFlag::DownstreamProtocolError)) {\n        stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::ProtocolError);\n      } else {\n        stream.response_encoder_->getStream().resetStream(StreamResetReason::LocalReset);\n      }\n    }\n    reset_stream = true;\n  }\n\n  if (!reset_stream) {\n    doDeferredStreamDestroy(stream);\n  }\n\n  if (reset_stream && codec_->protocol() < Protocol::Http2) {\n    drain_state_ = DrainState::Closing;\n  }\n\n  if (check_for_deferred_close) {\n     trailers_added_entry == decoder_filters_.end()) {\n      end_stream = false;\n      trailers_added_entry = entry;\n    }\n\n    // The decoder filter chain is finished here if the following is true:\n    // 1. the last filter has observed the end_stream AND\n    // 2. no filter, including the last filter, has injected trailers during header iteration.\n    //    NOTE: end_stream is set to false above if a filter injected trailers.\n    // If trailers were injected the end_stream will be processed in the `decodeTrailers()` method\n    // below.\n    terminal_filter_decoded_end_stream = end_stream && std::next(entry) == decoder_filters_.end();\n\n    if (!(*entry)->commonHandleAfterDataCallback(status, data, state_.decoder_filters_streaming_) &&\n        std::next(entry) != decoder_filters_.end()) {\n      // Stop iteration IFF this is not the last filter. If it is the last filter, continue with\n      // processing since we need to handle the case where a terminal filter wants to buffer, but\n      // a previous filter has added trailers.\n      break;\n    }\n  }\n\n  // If trailers were adding during decodeData we need to trigger decodeTrailers in order\n  // to allow filters to process the trailers.\n  if (trailers_added_entry != decoder_filters_.end()) {\n    decodeTrailers(trailers_added_entry->get(), *filter_manager_callbacks_.requestTrailers());\n  }\n\n  if (end_stream) {\n    disarmRequestTimeout();\n  }\n  maybeEndDecode(terminal_filter_decoded_end_stream);\n}\n\nRequestTrailerMap& FilterManager::addDecodedTrailers() {\n  // Trailers can only be added during the last data frame (i.e. end_stream = true).\n  ASSERT(state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::EndOfStream);\n\n  filter_manager_callbacks_.setRequestTrailers(RequestTrailerMapImpl::create());\n  return *filter_manager_callbacks_.requestTrailers();\n}\n\nvoid FilterManager::addDecodedData(ActiveStreamDecoderFilter& filter, Buffer::Instance& data,\n                                   bool streaming) {\n  if (state_.filter_call_state_ == 0 ||\n      (state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeHeaders) ||\n      (state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeData) ||\n      ((state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers) && !filter.canIterate())) {\n    // Make sure if this triggers watermarks, the correct action is taken.\n    state_.decoder_filters_streaming_ = streaming;\n    // If no call is happening or we are in the decode headers/data callback, buffer the data.\n    // Inline processing happens in the decodeHeaders() callback if necessary.\n    filter.commonHandleBufferData(data);\n  } else if (state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers) {\n    // In this case we need to inline dispatch the data to further filters. If those filters\n    // choose to buffer/stop iteration that's fine.\n    decodeData(&filter, data, false, FilterIterationStartState::AlwaysStartFromNext);\n  } else {\n    IS_ENVOY_BUG(\"Invalid request data\");\n    sendLocalReply(Http::Code::BadGateway, \"Filter error\", nullptr, absl::nullopt,\n                   StreamInfo::ResponseCodeDetails::get().FilterAddedInvalidRequestData);\n  }\n}\n\nMetadataMapVector& FilterManager::addDecodedMetadata() { return *getRequestMetadataMapVector(); }\n\nvoid FilterManager::decodeTrailers(ActiveStreamDecoderFilter* filter, RequestTrailerMap& trailers) {\n  // If a response is complete or a reset has been sent, filters do not care about further body\n  // data. Just drop it.\n  if (stopDecoderFilterChain()) {\n    return;\n  }\n\n  // Filter iteration may start at the current filter.\n  StreamDecoderFilters::Iterator entry =\n      commonDecodePrefix(filter, FilterIterationStartState::CanStartFromCurrent);\n  bool terminal_filter_reached = false;\n  ASSERT(!state_.decoder_filter_chain_complete_ || entry == decoder_filters_.end());\n\n  for (; entry != decoder_filters_.end(); entry++) {\n    ENVOY_EXECUTION_SCOPE(trackedStream(), &(*entry)->filter_context_);\n    // If the filter pointed by entry has stopped for all frame type, return now.\n    if ((*entry)->stoppedAll()) {\n      return;\n    }\n    ASSERT(!(state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers));\n    state_.filter_call_state_ |= FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers;\n    FilterTrailersStatus status = (*entry)->handle_->decodeTrailers(trailers);\n    (*entry)->handle_->decodeComplete();\n    (*entry)->end_stream_ = true;\n    state_.filter_call_state_ &= ~FilterCallState::DecodeTrailers;\n    ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(trace, \"decode trailers called: filter={} status={}\", *this,\n                     (*entry)->filter_context_.config_name, static_cast<uint64_t>(status));\n    if (state_.decoder_filter_chain_aborted_) {\n      executeLocalReplyIfPrepared();\n      ENVOY_STREAM_LOG(trace,\n                       \"decodeTrailers filter iteration aborted due to local reply: filter={}\",\n                       *this, (*entry)->filter_context_.config_name);\n      status = FilterTrailersStatus::StopIteration;\n    }\n\n    processNewlyAddedMetadata();\n    // Check if the last filter has processed trailers\n    terminal_filter_reached = std::next(entry) == decoder_filters_.end();\n\n    if (!(*entry)->commonHandleAfterTrailersCallback(status) && !terminal_filter_reached) {\n      return;\n    }\n  }\n  disarmRequestTimeout();\n  maybeEndDecode(terminal_filter_reached);\n}\n\nvoid FilterManager::decodeMetadata(ActiveStreamDecoderFilter* filter, MetadataMap& metadata_map) {\n  ScopeTrackerScopeState scope(&*this, dispatcher_);\n  filter_manager_callbacks_.resetIdleTimer();\n\n  // Filter iteration may start at the current filter.\n  StreamDecoderFilters::Iterator entry =\n      commonDecodePrefix(filter, FilterIterationStartState::CanStartFromCurrent);\n\n  ASSERT(!(state_.filter_call_state_ & FilterCallState::DecodeMetadata));\n\n  for (; entry != decoder_filters_.end(); entry++) {\n    ENVOY_EXECUTION_SCOPE(trackedStream(), &(*entry)->filter_context_);\n    // If the filter pointed by entry has stopped for all frame type, stores metadata and returns.\n    // If the filter pointed by entry hasn't returned from decodeHeaders, stores newly added\n    // metadata in case decodeHeaders returns StopAllIteration. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01KCutuEGjNLgHJ5LRpLkoXH","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01LU9avVFaxnYxN9m5VWnSRr","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/coverage_analysis.md","content":"# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager\n\n## Summary\n\nAnalysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (2,607 lines),\n`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` (1,989 lines), and\n`source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` (542 lines) against the test suite\nin `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` (~5,400+ lines across three\ntest files) reveals six significant coverage gaps.\n\nThe most critical are: (1) the premature RST stream DoS-protection mechanism\n(`maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` + `isPrematureRstStream`) which has **zero\ntest coverage**, (2) the non-graceful path of `sendGoAwayAndClose`, and (3) the\nbranch in `encodeHeaders` where the UHV header-validator returns a *new\ntransformed* response header map. These three gaps can hide serious correctness\nbugs — including connection-state corruption and silent header-manipulation\nerrors — that cannot be caught by the existing test suite.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Premature RST Stream Detection and Connection Drain Protection\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~677–749\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: Two related, entirely untested functions protect against a\n  slow-RST DoS attack. `isPrematureRstStream` (lines 677–698) decides whether a\n  just-completed stream counts as a premature reset by checking whether it\n  finished before a configurable lifetime threshold and without sending a\n  response status. `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` (lines 700–749) is called\n  after every stream destruction and drains the connection (via\n  `doConnectionClose(Abort, ...)`) when more than 50 % of total streams have\n  been classified as premature. A recursion guard flag\n  (`drained_due_to_premature_resets_`) prevents the drain from triggering\n  infinite recursion through the `onResetStream → doDeferredStreamDestroy →\n  maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` call chain. No test in any of the three test\n  files exercises these functions; searches for `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`,\n  `isPrematureRstStream`, `premature_reset`, `PrematureReset`,\n  `drained_due_to_premature_resets_`, and\n  `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` all return no matches.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `PrematureRstStreamTriggersDrainAndConnectionClose`\n\n  *Setup*: Use an HTTP/2 mock codec. Create N streams where each stream resets\n  immediately without ever receiving a response (simulating premature RST\n  floods). Drive `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` past the runtime\n  key `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count` (default 500) while keeping\n  the ratio of premature resets above 50 %. A simpler variant uses the\n  early-close heuristic: fire enough resets that `number_premature_stream_resets_\n  * 2 >= limit` before reaching the total-count limit.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.value()` equals 1.\n  - `connection_.close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, \"too_many_premature_resets\")`\n    was called exactly once.\n  - A second call to `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` after the drain does\n    nothing (recursion guard: no additional `close` calls).\n\n  *Second sub-test* `IsPrematureRstStreamWithResponseCodeIsNotPremature`: Create\n  a stream, complete it with a 200 response, then destroy it. Verify that\n  `number_premature_stream_resets_` does **not** increment.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Without test coverage the following bugs can go undetected:\n  - Off-by-one or wrong operator in the 50 % ratio check at lines 731 and 735\n    allows an attacker to sustain a RST flood without triggering the drain.\n  - A bug in `isPrematureRstStream` could mis-classify every completed stream as\n    premature (or never premature), completely defeating the protection.\n  - The recursion guard `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` prevents a stack\n    overflow; if it were accidentally inverted or removed, production deployments\n    could crash under heavy reset traffic.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Non-Graceful `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` Path\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~797–824\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: `sendGoAwayAndClose` (lines 797–824) has two distinct\n  branches: graceful (`graceful=true`, lines 808–815) and immediate\n  (`graceful=false`, lines 816–823). The graceful path (which calls\n  `startDrainSequence()` and defers the actual close to `onDrainTimeout`) is\n  exercised by the existing test `SendGoAwayAndCloseGraceful`. The immediate\n  path — which calls `codec_->shutdownNotice()`, `codec_->goAway()`, then\n  `doConnectionClose(FlushWriteAndDelay, absl::nullopt, \"forced_goaway\")`\n  synchronously — has no corresponding test. Also untested: the `go_away_sent_`\n  guard that suppresses duplicate calls (lines 800–802), which applies equally\n  to both paths.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediate`\n\n  *Setup*: HTTP/2 mock codec. Install a decoder filter that calls\n  `callbacks_->sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` from within `decodeHeaders`.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `codec_->shutdownNotice()` called exactly once.\n  - `codec_->goAway()` called exactly once.\n  - `connection_.close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::FlushWriteAndDelay,\n    \"forced_goaway\")` called exactly once.\n  - Calling `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` a second time (simulating a re-entrant\n    or duplicate call) triggers **no** additional close calls (`go_away_sent_`\n    guard works).\n  - No drain timer is created (unlike the graceful path, which creates one).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The immediate close path is the \"emergency\" shutdown\n  used when the proxy detects a protocol violation or critical upstream failure\n  mid-stream. A bug here (e.g., missing `goAway()` call or wrong close type)\n  means the client is not properly notified that the connection is being\n  terminated, which can cause the client to retry on a half-closed connection\n  and trigger protocol-level errors. The `go_away_sent_` duplicate-call guard is\n  also entirely untested; if it were wrong, filters could trigger cascading\n  connection close calls.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Response Header Validator Returning Transformed (`new_headers`) Headers\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~2014–2024\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: At the bottom of `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders`, if a UHV\n  (Universal Header Validator) is configured, the code calls\n  `header_validator_->transformResponseHeaders(headers)` and then checks the\n  result (lines 2014–2024):\n\n  ```cpp\n  if (header_validator_) {\n    auto result = header_validator_->transformResponseHeaders(headers);\n    if (!result.status.ok()) {\n      // TODO(yanavlasov): add handling for this case.\n    } else if (result.new_headers) {\n      response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(*result.new_headers, end_stream);\n      return;\n    }\n  }\n  response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream);\n  ```\n\n  The existing test infrastructure (`expectUhvHeaderCheck`) always configures\n  `transformResponseHeaders` to return `ResponseHeadersTransformationResult::success()`\n  (i.e., `{RejectResult::success(), nullptr}`), so the `result.new_headers`\n  branch is never reached. Similarly, the `!result.status.ok()` failure branch\n  (marked with a TODO) is never reached or tested.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ResponseHeaderValidatorTransformationProducesNewHeaders`\n\n  *Setup*: Enable UHV via `header_validator_factory_`. Configure\n  `transformResponseHeaders` to return a `ResponseHeadersTransformationResult`\n  where `new_headers` is a non-null `ResponseHeaderMapPtr` containing a modified\n  `:status` header (e.g., replacing `200` with `200` but adding a\n  `content-type` header). Dispatch a normal request and have the upstream filter\n  call `encodeHeaders`.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders(...)` is called with the **new** header map\n    (containing the added `content-type`), not the original.\n  - `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders(...)` is called exactly once (the early\n    `return` after encoding `new_headers` prevents a double encode).\n\n  *Second sub-test* `ResponseHeaderValidatorTransformationFailureIsIgnored`:\n  Configure `transformResponseHeaders` to return\n  `{RejectResult::reject(\"invalid\"), nullptr}` (failure without new headers).\n  Verify that encoding falls through to the original headers (documenting the\n  current missing-handler behavior).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The `new_headers` path is the intended mechanism for\n  HTTP/2-to-HTTP/1 upgrade response translation (e.g., converting an extended\n  CONNECT response back to an HTTP/1.1 Upgrade response). Without a test, two\n  classes of bugs are invisible: (1) the early `return` could be accidentally\n  removed, causing the original (potentially invalid) headers to also be sent,\n  corrupting the wire protocol; (2) the TODO failure path has no handling at all\n  — if a validator marks a response as invalid, the proxy silently forwards it\n  anyway, which violates security and correctness guarantees.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: `chargeStats()` Skips Statistics for Internal Redirects\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1078–1103\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::chargeStats` (lines 1063–1104) is responsible\n  for incrementing downstream response statistics (`downstream_rq_completed_`,\n  `downstream_rq_2xx_`, etc.). Lines 1078–1083 contain an early-return guard:\n\n  ```cpp\n  const absl::optional<std::string>& response_code_details =\n      filter_manager_.streamInfo().responseCodeDetails();\n  if (response_code_details.has_value() &&\n      response_code_details == ResponseCodeDetails::get().InternalRedirect) {\n    return;\n  }\n  ```\n\n  When a request is internally redirected, `encodeHeaders` is still called\n  (with the redirect response), which calls `chargeStats`. The guard prevents\n  double-counting the response since the redirected stream will be charged\n  separately. No test verifies: (a) that `downstream_rq_completed_` is NOT\n  incremented for an internally-redirected stream, or (b) that the final\n  redirected stream IS charged correctly.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `InternalRedirectDoesNotChargeDownstreamStats`\n\n  *Setup*: Use a decoder filter that sets `response_code_details` to\n  `ResponseCodeDetails::get().InternalRedirect` on the stream info, then calls\n  `encodeHeaders` with a 307 response.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_completed_.value()` equals 0 after the\n    redirected encode.\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_3xx_.value()` equals 0 after the redirected\n    encode.\n  - A subsequent normal (non-redirect) encode correctly increments both counters\n    to 1 (validating the full flow).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: If the `InternalRedirect` guard were accidentally removed\n  or its string comparison broken (e.g., by a rename of the constant),\n  `downstream_rq_completed_` would be incremented for every redirect hop,\n  causing overcounting in dashboards and alerting systems. In high-redirect\n  configurations this could cause misleading SLO metrics. Conversely, if the\n  guard were too broad, legitimate responses might not be counted.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: HTTP/1.0 `Connection: keep-alive` Injection in `encodeHeaders`\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1938–1948\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders` contains special handling for\n  HTTP/1.0 connections (lines 1938–1948):\n\n  ```cpp\n  if (connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http10) {\n    if (!headers.ContentLength()) {\n      filter_manager_.streamInfo().setShouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion(true);\n    }\n    if (!filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()) {\n      headers.setConnection(Headers::get().ConnectionValues.KeepAlive);\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n\n  When an HTTP/1.0 response includes a `Content-Length` header (allowing\n  keep-alive framing), Envoy injects `Connection: keep-alive` to signal to the\n  client that the connection will not be closed. While there are tests for\n  `ResponseBeforeRequestComplete10` that check the close behavior when there is\n  no Content-Length, no test verifies the keep-alive injection branch (the path\n  taken when `Content-Length` is present).\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `Http10ResponseWithContentLengthInjectsKeepAlive`\n\n  *Setup*: Configure the mock codec to return `Protocol::Http10`. Dispatch a\n  request. In the filter's response path, call `encodeHeaders` with a\n  response that includes a `content-length: 42` header.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - The `Connection` header in the encoded response equals `\"keep-alive\"`.\n  - `filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` is\n    false (connection is kept open).\n  - `connection_.close(...)` is NOT called after the response completes.\n\n  *Companion test* `Http10ResponseWithoutContentLengthClosesConnection`:\n  Verify the inverse: no `Content-Length` → `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion`\n  set to true → `connection_.close(...)` called.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: HTTP/1.0 clients rely on `Connection: keep-alive` to\n  decide whether to reuse the TCP connection. If Envoy fails to inject this\n  header, clients may close the connection unnecessarily (degrading performance),\n  or worse, may reuse a connection that Envoy has already marked for closure,\n  leading to request failures. The dual behavior (keep-alive vs. drain-on-close)\n  is entirely untested for the keep-alive path.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: `validateTrailers()` HTTP/2 `InvalidUnderscore` Sends Stream Reset, Not 400\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1281–1298\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::validateTrailers` (lines 1256–1299) contains\n  a protocol-version-specific branch at lines 1282–1298. When trailer validation\n  fails with `UhvResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidUnderscore`:\n\n  ```cpp\n  if (failure_details == UhvResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidUnderscore &&\n      connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http2) {\n    filter_manager_.streamInfo().setResponseCodeDetails(failure_details);\n    resetStream();      // <-- HTTP/2 resets stream\n  } else {\n    if (connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() < Protocol::Http2) {\n      sendLocalReply(response_code, \"\", nullptr, grpc_status, failure_details); // HTTP/1 sends 400\n    } else {\n      resetStream();    // Other HTTP/2 errors also reset\n    }\n    if (!response_encoder_->streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()) {\n      connection_manager_.handleCodecError(failure_details);\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n\n  Tests exist for HTTP/1.1 trailer validation rejection\n  (`HeaderValidatorRejectTrailersBeforeResponseHttp1`) and HTTP/2 general\n  rejection (`HeaderValidatorRejectTrailersBeforeResponseHttp2`), but no test\n  covers the specific `InvalidUnderscore` case for HTTP/2 trailers, which takes\n  a slightly different code path (skips the `handleCodecError` call).\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `TrailerValidatorRejectUnderscoreHttp2ResetsStreamOnly`\n\n  *Setup*: Use HTTP/2 mock codec. Enable UHV trailer validation. Configure\n  `validateRequestTrailers` to return a failure with\n  `UhvResponseCodeDetail::get().InvalidUnderscore`. Dispatch a request with\n  trailers after a partial body.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `resetStream()` is called (not `sendLocalReply` with 400).\n  - `connection_.close(...)` (via `handleCodecError`) is NOT called — the\n    stream reset is stream-level, not connection-level.\n  - The stream info `responseCodeDetails` equals `InvalidUnderscore`.\n  - Compare with the HTTP/1.1 case: same `InvalidUnderscore` failure triggers\n    a 400 local reply AND a connection close.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The HTTP/2 `InvalidUnderscore` path intentionally omits\n  `handleCodecError` (which would close the connection), matching historical\n  nghttp2 behavior. A regression that accidentally routes this through\n  `handleCodecError` would cause entire HTTP/2 connections to be torn down on a\n  single bad trailer, causing amplified client impact. Since HTTP/2 multiplexes\n  many requests per connection, this is a correctness and availability concern.\n\n---\n\n## File References\n\n| File | Lines | Role |\n|------|-------|------|\n| `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` | 2,607 | Primary HCM implementation |\n| `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` | 1,989 | Filter chain execution |\n| `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` | 542 | Header map implementation |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc` | 5,407 | Primary test file |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_2.cc` | ~2,280 | Secondary test file |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_3.cc` | ~2,840 | Third test file |\n| `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test_base.cc` | 571 | Test base/mixin |\n| `envoy/http/header_validator.h` | — | UHV interface definitions |\n\n### Key Symbols Cross-Referenced\n\n| Symbol | Location | Tested? {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01LU9avVFaxnYxN9m5VWnSRr","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /workspace/coverage_analysis.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"75fb0246-9619-446a-a5ed-814717fc2445","uuid":"f8416fd5-5a7a-49d2-a464-d9e6a82f1d5c","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/workspace/coverage_analysis.md","content":"# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager\n\n## Summary\n\nAnalysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (2,607 lines),\n`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` (1,989 lines), and\n`source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` (542 lines) against the test suite\nin `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test*.cc` (~5,400+ lines across three\ntest files) reveals six significant coverage gaps.\n\nThe most critical are: (1) the premature RST stream DoS-protection mechanism\n(`maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` + `isPrematureRstStream`) which has **zero\ntest coverage**, (2) the non-graceful path of `sendGoAwayAndClose`, and (3) the\nbranch in `encodeHeaders` where the UHV header-validator returns a *new\ntransformed* response header map. These three gaps can hide serious correctness\nbugs — including connection-state corruption and silent header-manipulation\nerrors — that cannot be caught by the existing test suite.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Premature RST Stream Detection and Connection Drain Protection\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~677–749\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: Two related, entirely untested functions protect against a\n  slow-RST DoS attack. `isPrematureRstStream` (lines 677–698) decides whether a\n  just-completed stream counts as a premature reset by checking whether it\n  finished before a configurable lifetime threshold and without sending a\n  response status. `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` (lines 700–749) is called\n  after every stream destruction and drains the connection (via\n  `doConnectionClose(Abort, ...)`) when more than 50 % of total streams have\n  been classified as premature. A recursion guard flag\n  (`drained_due_to_premature_resets_`) prevents the drain from triggering\n  infinite recursion through the `onResetStream → doDeferredStreamDestroy →\n  maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` call chain. No test in any of the three test\n  files exercises these functions; searches for `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`,\n  `isPrematureRstStream`, `premature_reset`, `PrematureReset`,\n  `drained_due_to_premature_resets_`, and\n  `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` all return no matches.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `PrematureRstStreamTriggersDrainAndConnectionClose`\n\n  *Setup*: Use an HTTP/2 mock codec. Create N streams where each stream resets\n  immediately without ever receiving a response (simulating premature RST\n  floods). Drive `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` past the runtime\n  key `overload.premature_reset_total_stream_count` (default 500) while keeping\n  the ratio of premature resets above 50 %. A simpler variant uses the\n  early-close heuristic: fire enough resets that `number_premature_stream_resets_\n  * 2 >= limit` before reaching the total-count limit.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.value()` equals 1.\n  - `connection_.close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, \"too_many_premature_resets\")`\n    was called exactly once.\n  - A second call to `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` after the drain does\n    nothing (recursion guard: no additional `close` calls).\n\n  *Second sub-test* `IsPrematureRstStreamWithResponseCodeIsNotPremature`: Create\n  a stream, complete it with a 200 response, then destroy it. Verify that\n  `number_premature_stream_resets_` does **not** increment.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: Without test coverage the following bugs can go undetected:\n  - Off-by-one or wrong operator in the 50 % ratio check at lines 731 and 735\n    allows an attacker to sustain a RST flood without triggering the drain.\n  - A bug in `isPrematureRstStream` could mis-classify every completed stream as\n    premature (or never premature), completely defeating the protection.\n  - The recursion guard `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` prevents a stack\n    overflow; if it were accidentally inverted or removed, production deployments\n    could crash under heavy reset traffic.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Non-Graceful `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` Path\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~797–824\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: `sendGoAwayAndClose` (lines 797–824) has two distinct\n  branches: graceful (`graceful=true`, lines 808–815) and immediate\n  (`graceful=false`, lines 816–823). The graceful path (which calls\n  `startDrainSequence()` and defers the actual close to `onDrainTimeout`) is\n  exercised by the existing test `SendGoAwayAndCloseGraceful`. The immediate\n  path — which calls `codec_->shutdownNotice()`, `codec_->goAway()`, then\n  `doConnectionClose(FlushWriteAndDelay, absl::nullopt, \"forced_goaway\")`\n  synchronously — has no corresponding test. Also untested: the `go_away_sent_`\n  guard that suppresses duplicate calls (lines 800–802), which applies equally\n  to both paths.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `SendGoAwayAndCloseImmediate`\n\n  *Setup*: HTTP/2 mock codec. Install a decoder filter that calls\n  `callbacks_->sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` from within `decodeHeaders`.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `codec_->shutdownNotice()` called exactly once.\n  - `codec_->goAway()` called exactly once.\n  - `connection_.close(Network::ConnectionCloseType::FlushWriteAndDelay,\n    \"forced_goaway\")` called exactly once.\n  - Calling `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` a second time (simulating a re-entrant\n    or duplicate call) triggers **no** additional close calls (`go_away_sent_`\n    guard works).\n  - No drain timer is created (unlike the graceful path, which creates one).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The immediate close path is the \"emergency\" shutdown\n  used when the proxy detects a protocol violation or critical upstream failure\n  mid-stream. A bug here (e.g., missing `goAway()` call or wrong close type)\n  means the client is not properly notified that the connection is being\n  terminated, which can cause the client to retry on a half-closed connection\n  and trigger protocol-level errors. The `go_away_sent_` duplicate-call guard is\n  also entirely untested; if it were wrong, filters could trigger cascading\n  connection close calls.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 3: Response Header Validator Returning Transformed (`new_headers`) Headers\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~2014–2024\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**: At the bottom of `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders`, if a UHV\n  (Universal Header Validator) is configured, the code calls\n  `header_validator_->transformResponseHeaders(headers)` and then checks the\n  result (lines 2014–2024):\n\n  ```cpp\n  if (header_validator_) {\n    auto result = header_validator_->transformResponseHeaders(headers);\n    if (!result.status.ok()) {\n      // TODO(yanavlasov): add handling for this case.\n    } else if (result.new_headers) {\n      response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(*result.new_headers, end_stream);\n      return;\n    }\n  }\n  response_encoder_->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream);\n  ```\n\n  The existing test infrastructure (`expectUhvHeaderCheck`) always configures\n  `transformResponseHeaders` to return `ResponseHeadersTransformationResult::success()`\n  (i.e., `{RejectResult::success(), nullptr}`), so the `result.new_headers`\n  branch is never reached. Similarly, the `!result.status.ok()` failure branch\n  (marked with a TODO) is never reached or tested.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `ResponseHeaderValidatorTransformationProducesNewHeaders`\n\n  *Setup*: Enable UHV via `header_validator_factory_`. Configure\n  `transformResponseHeaders` to return a `ResponseHeadersTransformationResult`\n  where `new_headers` is a non-null `ResponseHeaderMapPtr` containing a modified\n  `:status` header (e.g., replacing `200` with `200` but adding a\n  `content-type` header). Dispatch a normal request and have the upstream filter\n  call `encodeHeaders`.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders(...)` is called with the **new** header map\n    (containing the added `content-type`), not the original.\n  - `response_encoder_.encodeHeaders(...)` is called exactly once (the early\n    `return` after encoding `new_headers` prevents a double encode).\n\n  *Second sub-test* `ResponseHeaderValidatorTransformationFailureIsIgnored`:\n  Configure `transformResponseHeaders` to return\n  `{RejectResult::reject(\"invalid\"), nullptr}` (failure without new headers).\n  Verify that encoding falls through to the original headers (documenting the\n  current missing-handler behavior).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: The `new_headers` path is the intended mechanism for\n  HTTP/2-to-HTTP/1 upgrade response translation (e.g., converting an extended\n  CONNECT response back to an HTTP/1.1 Upgrade response). Without a test, two\n  classes of bugs are invisible: (1) the early `return` could be accidentally\n  removed, causing the original (potentially invalid) headers to also be sent,\n  corrupting the wire protocol; (2) the TODO failure path has no handling at all\n  — if a validator marks a response as invalid, the proxy silently forwards it\n  anyway, which violates security and correctness guarantees.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 4: `chargeStats()` Skips Statistics for Internal Redirects\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1078–1103\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::chargeStats` (lines 1063–1104) is responsible\n  for incrementing downstream response statistics (`downstream_rq_completed_`,\n  `downstream_rq_2xx_`, etc.). Lines 1078–1083 contain an early-return guard:\n\n  ```cpp\n  const absl::optional<std::string>& response_code_details =\n      filter_manager_.streamInfo().responseCodeDetails();\n  if (response_code_details.has_value() &&\n      response_code_details == ResponseCodeDetails::get().InternalRedirect) {\n    return;\n  }\n  ```\n\n  When a request is internally redirected, `encodeHeaders` is still called\n  (with the redirect response), which calls `chargeStats`. The guard prevents\n  double-counting the response since the redirected stream will be charged\n  separately. No test verifies: (a) that `downstream_rq_completed_` is NOT\n  incremented for an internally-redirected stream, or (b) that the final\n  redirected stream IS charged correctly.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `InternalRedirectDoesNotChargeDownstreamStats`\n\n  *Setup*: Use a decoder filter that sets `response_code_details` to\n  `ResponseCodeDetails::get().InternalRedirect` on the stream info, then calls\n  `encodeHeaders` with a 307 response.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_completed_.value()` equals 0 after the\n    redirected encode.\n  - `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_3xx_.value()` equals 0 after the redirected\n    encode.\n  - A subsequent normal (non-redirect) encode correctly increments both counters\n    to 1 (validating the full flow).\n\n- **Why It Matters**: If the `InternalRedirect` guard were accidentally removed\n  or its string comparison broken (e.g., by a rename of the constant),\n  `downstream_rq_completed_` would be incremented for every redirect hop,\n  causing overcounting in dashboards and alerting systems. In high-redirect\n  configurations this could cause misleading SLO metrics. Conversely, if the\n  guard were too broad, legitimate responses might not be counted.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 5: HTTP/1.0 `Connection: keep-alive` Injection in `encodeHeaders`\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1938–1948\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::encodeHeaders` contains special handling for\n  HTTP/1.0 connections (lines 1938–1948):\n\n  ```cpp\n  if (connection_manager_.codec_->protocol() == Protocol::Http10) {\n    if (!headers.ContentLength()) {\n      filter_manager_.streamInfo().setShouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion(true);\n    }\n    if (!filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()) {\n      headers.setConnection(Headers::get().ConnectionValues.KeepAlive);\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n\n  When an HTTP/1.0 response includes a `Content-Length` header (allowing\n  keep-alive framing), Envoy injects `Connection: keep-alive` to signal to the\n  client that the connection will not be closed. While there are tests for\n  `ResponseBeforeRequestComplete10` that check the close behavior when there is\n  no Content-Length, no test verifies the keep-alive injection branch (the path\n  taken when `Content-Length` is present).\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `Http10ResponseWithContentLengthInjectsKeepAlive`\n\n  *Setup*: Configure the mock codec to return `Protocol::Http10`. Dispatch a\n  request. In the filter's response path, call `encodeHeaders` with a\n  response that includes a `content-length: 42` header.\n\n  *Assertions*:\n  - The `Connection` header in the encoded response equals `\"keep-alive\"`.\n  - `filter_manager_.streamInfo().shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion()` is\n    false (connection is kept open).\n  - `connection_.close(...)` is NOT called after the response completes.\n\n  *Companion test* `Http10ResponseWithoutContentLengthClosesConnection`:\n  Verify the inverse: no `Content-Length` → `shouldDrainConnectionUponCompletion`\n  set to true → `connection_.close(...)` called.\n\n- **Why It Matters**: HTTP/1.0 clients rely on `Connection: keep-alive` to\n  decide whether to reuse the TCP connection. If Envoy fails to inject this\n  header, clients may close the connection unnecessarily (degrading performance),\n  or worse, may reuse a connection that Envoy has already marked for closure,\n  leading to request failures. The dual behavior (keep-alive vs. drain-on-close)\n  is entirely untested for the keep-alive path.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 6: `validateTrailers()` HTTP/2 `InvalidUnderscore` Sends Stream Reset, Not 400\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~1281–1298\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**: `ActiveStream::validateTrailers` (lines 1256–1299) contains\n  a protocol-version-specific branch at lines 1282–1298.
